                  <hi rend="ital">Having</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حِلْم</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">forbearance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">clemency,</hi> &amp;c.; <hi rend="ital">forbearing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">clement,</hi> &amp;c.]: (Mgh, Msb, K:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">حُلَمَآءُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَحْلَامٌ</foreign>. (K.) In the Kur xi. 89, it is said to be used by way of scoffing [or irony]. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">الحَلِيمُ</foreign> is one of the names of God; meaning [<hi rend="ital">The Forbearing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">Clement,</hi> &amp;c.; or] <hi rend="ital">He Whom the disobedience of the disobedient does not flurry, nor anger against them disquiet, but Who has appointed to everything a term to which it must finally come.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَلِيمَةٌ مُغْتَاظَةٌ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [lit. <hi rend="ital">Calm, angry;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like;</hi> because what it contains is sometimes still and sometimes boiling;] is an appellation given to <hi rend="ital">a stone cooking-pot.</hi> (A and TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">غيظ</foreign>.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  A <hi rend="ital">fat</hi> camel: (S:) or a camel <hi rend="ital">becoming fat.</hi> (ISd, K.) ISd says, I know not any unaugmented verb belonging to it in this sense.
